    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">

    in the 16&quot;. It is nice to compare M35-M38 because they are quite close to

    500 total, spread over an area the size of the full moon.</td>

    <td valign="top" style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">Aur</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">6.5</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana">&nbsp;&nbsp;2/13/09</font></td>
    <td valign="bottom" style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in" align="left">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    There are 3 clusters lying fairly close together in Auiga, M36, 37 and 38.
    This one is the most sparse. It is primarily a few dozen bright stars,
    perhaps of slightly different hues (yellow-orange). Otherwise, not terribly
    interesting, and I don't see why its called the pinwheel..</td>
  </tr>
  <tr style="height: 14.05pt">
    <td valign="top" style="width: 48; height: 43; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;

    <p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;

    <span style="font-size:10.0pt">Auriga Salt-and-pepper Cluster</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 99; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;

    <td valign="top" style="width: 40; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">Aur</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 33; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">6</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 65; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana">&nbsp;&nbsp;2/13/09</font></td>
    <td valign="bottom" style="width: 240; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in" align="left">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    Very nice open cluster. A rich field of dim stars sprinkled like salt (and
    pepper?). Fairly large cluster (easily fills 50mm in 16&quot;). Worth seeing in
    finder scope as well.</td>
  </tr>

    <td valign="top" style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
  margin-left:0in" align="center"><font face="Verdana">
    <span style="font-size:10.0pt">Dbl+Asterism</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">Uma</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">8.7</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana">2/14/09&nbsp;</font></td>
    <td valign="bottom" style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in" align="left">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    This object is a rather uninteresting double star as the separation is not
    very close. It is believed to in fact be an optical double. Measurements
    show the stars are moving apart, and have moved significantly in the last
    century. In all likelihood, this was a mistake in Messer's list, he was
    trying to find a non-existent nebula reported to be near this double. (see
    link for more info).</td>
  </tr>

    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">

    adjacent to M42 with faint nebulosity around it. Both this and the center of
    the Orion Nebula can fit in the same FOV in the 16&quot;. </td>

    <td valign="top" style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">

    <td valign="bottom" style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in" align="left">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    This object is sort of a mystery to me... it is apparently part of an array
    of reflection nebula in the Orion complex, and the brightest reflection
    nebula in the N. Hemisphere. It lies above the leftmost star in Orion's
    belt. It should be very easy to spot under dark skies, but I'm not really
    sure of the scale of the thing. Starry night shows it being as very small,
    but it is listed as 8x6 arc mins and looks pretty big. </td>

    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">Leo</span></font></td>

    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">10.6</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana">&nbsp;2/14/09</font></td>
    <td valign="bottom" style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in" align="left">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    M95 and M96 are both excellent galaxies. Despite a low integrated magnitude,
    these objects where relatively easy to spot, given a clear, dark night. This
    is probably because they are relatively small.&nbsp; Both can be seen in the
    50mm eyepiece at the same time, and its quite a sight to see. </td>

    <td valign="top" style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
  margin-left:0in" align="center"><font face="Verdana">
    <span style="font-size:10.0pt">Galaxy</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">And</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana"><span style="font-size:10.0pt">8.9</span></font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in" align="center">
    <font face="Verdana">&nbsp;9/12/07</font></td>
    <td valign="top" style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in" align="left">
    <p class="Default" style="margin: 4.0pt 0in">
    &nbsp;Visible in 3&quot; finder scope on 16&quot; under good conditions.&nbsp; </td>
  </tr>

  </center>

<p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:0in" align="center">
<b><font size="4">Planets &amp; Moons</font></b></p>
<div align="center">
  <center>
<table border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="border-collapse: collapse" bordercolor="#111111" width="61%" height="153">
  <tr>
    <td width="7%" height="18"><b>Planet</b></td>
    <td width="9%" height="18"><b>Mag</b></td>
    <td width="8%" height="18"><b>Date</b></td>
    <td width="28%" height="18"><b>Notes</b></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="7%" height="25">Mercury</td>
    <td width="9%" height="25">-1.9</td>
    <td width="8%" height="25">11/08</td>
    <td width="28%" height="25"><font face="Times New Roman">Was walking back to
    car at Highland Meadows when I happened to see Mercury by chance during a
    conjunction with Jupiter at sunset. (A very striking combination.. which I
    verified afterwards with Starry Night). This is a rather tricky object to
    view.. you have to be somewhere with an open western horizon at just the
    right time after sunset... or get up really early in the morning and have a
    clear eastern horizon. I hope to observe again through telescope during
    maximum elongation. </font> </td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="7%" height="18">Venus</td>
    <td width="9%" height="18">-3.7 - -4.7</td>
    <td width="8%" height="18">?</td>
    <td width="28%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">Varies in size and brightness. Not much to see
    other than phases. Have not yet seen the &quot;Ashen glow&quot; phenomena. I have not
    been able to see it with the naked eye during the day, but others have. This
    is a good object to view with the 16&quot; during Solar Observing, if there are
    large crowds. During March 2009, we were able to discern the crescent shape
    with the naked eye.</font></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="7%" height="18">Earth</td>
    <td width="9%" height="18">7 - -26.73</td>
    <td width="8%" height="18">3/6/88</td>
    <td width="28%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">Don't forget Earth!</font></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="7%" height="18">Mars</td>
    <td width="9%" height="18">1.8 - -2.91</td>
    <td width="8%" height="18">?</td>
    <td width="28%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">I haven't had much success with Mars...
    it looks nice and red.. but otherwise quite disappointing. Its a shame,
    because its my favorite planet (after Earth of course). </font></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="7%" height="18">Jupiter</td>
    <td width="9%" height="18">-1.6 - -2.94<p></td>

    <td width="28%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">Cloud bands and great red spot visible in 6&quot; along
    with
    4 Galilean moons. Shadow of Io was visible in 6&quot; at ADK star party.
    Shadow has also been observed in 16&quot;. Very
    good object for 16&quot; once it gets high in the sky.&nbsp; </font> </td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="7%" height="18">Saturn</td>
    <td width="9%" height="18">+1.2 - -0.24</td>

    seen Cassini division several times under good conditions as well as 5
    brightest moons, Titan, Tethys, Dione, Rhea and Iapetus.</font></td>

<p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:0in" align="center">
<b><font size="4">Comets</font></b></p>
<div align="center">
  <center>
<table border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="border-collapse: collapse" bordercolor="#111111" width="60%" height="59">
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="1"><b>Name</b></td>
    <td width="4%" height="1"><b>Mag</b></td>
    <td width="1%" height="1"><b>Date</b></td>
    <td width="43%" height="1"><b>Notes</b></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="1">
    <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet_Holmes">17P/Holmes</a></td>
    <td width="4%" height="1">2.8-3</td>
    <td width="1%" height="1">10/11/08</td>
    <td width="43%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">Normally dim comet which had spectacular outburst. Visible
    with naked eye for several weeks. It appeared as a star with nebulosity at
    first, but eventually expanded and lost brightness, eventually it was half
    the size of moon. The bright core was easily visible in 16&quot; a few days after
    the outburst. Slight fragmentation may have been observed around the
    nucleus, although this was never confirmed. (Technically, the nucleolus is
    too small to be visible, what one sees is an bright inner coma). The overall halo structure was easily seen in binoculars and very
    impressive in the 3&quot; finder. </font> </td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="23">
    <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading"><span style="font-weight: 400">
    <font size="3"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C/2007_N3">C/2007 N3
    Lulin</a></font></span></h1>
&nbsp;</td>
    <td width="4%" height="23">~7-8</td>
    <td width="1%" height="23">2/24/09</td>
    <td width="43%" height="23"><font face="Times New Roman">Many hoped that
    Comet Lulin would reach naked eye visibility. In the end it was not quite
    bright enough, except under perfectly dark skies. At RPI&nbsp; there was no
    chance of visual observation but it could be seen fairly easily with binoculars.
    I first spotted it with Dave's 10&quot; lying just above Saturn. As the night
    progressed it moved quite noticeably on a path from Saturn towards Regulus.
    It was quite bright in the 16&quot;, but it did not have very much of a comet-like
    appearance; appearing as a bright cloud with a semi-circular coma. After
    careful inspection, it was clear that  coma
    was in fact elliptical and extending off both sides.&nbsp; This overall indistinctness of the tail was
    due to the fact that the comet was moving towards us in the plane of the
    earth's orbit, and the tail was fanning out behind it. A subsequent
    observation was made that Saturday, 3/1/09 and it had dimmed quite
    noticeably in the 16&quot;. By that time it had already passed Regulus and was
    headed through Cancer towards Gemini. I observed it again on 3/20/09 while
    it was in Gemini , and it had dimmed down to magnitude 8.6 but was still
    fairly easy to spot in the 16&quot;. It had shrunk to at most half, maybe a
    quarter of its original size, and appeared a little bit more elongated.
    Still, it was very dim and fuzzy, and there was nothing about it by which
    was distinctly cometary in nature.&nbsp; We had to check to make sure we
    were not actually looking at a globular cluster or galaxy that happened to
    be nearby. </font></td>
  </tr>
  </table>
  </center>
</div>
<p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:0in" align="center">

<p class="Default" style="margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:0in" align="center">
<font size="4"><b>Spacecraft</b></font></p>
<div align="center">
  <center>
<table border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="border-collapse: collapse" bordercolor="#111111" width="60%" height="59">
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="1"><b>Name</b></td>
    <td width="5%" height="1"><b>Mag</b></td>
    <td width="5%" height="1"><b>Date</b></td>
    <td width="39%" height="1"><b>Notes</b></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="1">
    <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iridium_flare">Iridium Flares</a></td>
    <td width="5%" height="1">-1to -8</td>
    <td width="5%" height="1">various</td>
    <td width="39%" height="1">&nbsp;<p>Iridium Flares are really cool! On at
    least one occasion I saw one reach magnitude -8, which is about as bright as
    they get.</p>
    <p>&nbsp;</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="23">
    <h1 id="firstHeading0" class="firstHeading"><br>
    <font size="3"><span style="font-weight: 400">
    <a href="http://heavens-above.com">International Space Station</a></span></font></h1>
    <p>&nbsp;</td>
    <td width="5%" height="23">-1 to -2 in 2007<p>-2 to -3 in 2009</td>
    <td width="5%" height="23">Various</td>
    <td width="39%" height="23">The ISS is very easy to see, and always a crowd
    pleaser. </td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="23">
    <h1 id="firstHeading0" class="firstHeading"><br>
    <font size="3"><span style="font-weight: 400">
    <a href="http://www.space.com/spacewatch/090310-space-shuttle-launch-spotting.html">
    Space Shuttle Discovery</a> (during launch)</span></font></h1>
    <p>&nbsp;</td>
    <td width="5%" height="23">around 0 to -1</td>
    <td width="5%" height="23">3-15-09</td>
    <td width="39%" height="23"><br>
    We had a special opportunity to view the Shuttle Launch, because it was an
    evening launch with clear skies. I was skeptical about whether we would see
    it from the Hirsch Observatory, and quite amazed when we did. The shuttle
    launched right on time at 7:43, which we watched indoors on NASA TV. Then we
    went out onto the roof and stood scanning the southern horizon with no
    avail. We had just about given up when a bright red glow object appeared
    moving very fast starting in the southeast. It flickered on and off several
    times. We later determined this must have been due to a large complex of
    clouds just south of Long Island. We tracked the shuttle for about 30
    seconds before main-engine cut off. <br>
&nbsp;</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td width="4%" height="23">
    <h1 id="firstHeading0" class="firstHeading"><br>
    <font size="3"><span style="font-weight: 400">
    <a href="http://www.space.com/spacewatch/090310-space-shuttle-launch-spotting.html">
    Space Shuttle Discovery</a> (In orbit)</span></font></h1>
    <p>&nbsp;</td>
    <td width="5%" height="23">around 2.5-3</td>
    <td width="5%" height="23">3-28-09</td>
    <td width="39%" height="23"><br>
    I was standing out on the roof when I noticed 2 objects moving along the
    same arc in the North. The first was quite bright, and due to the gentle
    curve of the arc, I immediately suspected it was the ISS, rather than a
    plane. The other object was about 1-1.5 degrees away, leading the ISS. I was
    very sure that was the shuttle, but others were skeptical. A quick check
    online showed that the shuttle had undocked from the ISS about 6 hours ago.&nbsp;
    <br>
&nbsp;</td>
  </tr>
  </table>
  </center>
</div>

However, due to the site design, I was not able to link directly to pages there. <br>

      <td width="17%" height="20">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albireo">Albireo </a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="20"><font face="Times New Roman">Beta Cygni</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="20"><font face="Times New Roman">Double Star</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="20"><font face="Times New Roman">3&amp;5</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="20"><font face="Times New Roman">2007</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="20"><font face="Times New Roman">Part of Cygnus, a bright double star with red
      and blue components. Imaged.</font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="18">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coathanger_cluster">Coathanger
      Cluster</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">Collinder 399</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">Asterism</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">3.6</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">2008</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">Also known as
      Brocchi's Cluster, it is an asterism (chance alignment), not a star
      cluster. It consists of 6 stars in a straight line, and a few other stars
      composing the hook of the &quot;coathanger&quot;.</font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="1"><a href="Epsilon%20Lyre">Double Double</a>&nbsp;
      </td>
      <td width="9%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">Epsilon Lyrae</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">Multiple Star</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">1.1</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">2007</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">Cool double double star. The first split can
      be seen with binoculars. The second split can be resolved in the 11&quot; and
      the 16&quot;. </font> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="1">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamma_Andromedae">Gamma Andromeda</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="1"></td>
      <td width="9%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">Double Star</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="1"><font face="Times New Roman">-2.9</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="1"></td>
      <td width="119%" height="1"> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="18">
      <a href="http://www.skyhound.com/sh/archive/dec/NGC_1664.html">Kite
      Cluster</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">NGC 1664</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">Open Cluster</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">7.2</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">8/22/08</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="18"><font face="Times New Roman">This is a small
      open cluster. The brightest stars resembled a diamond or &quot;kite&quot;. The
      density of surrounding stars did not seem above normal, so it seemed like
      more like an asterism to me. Observed at ADK star party. </font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://www.seds.org/messier/xtra/ngc/n2362.html">The Mexican
      Jumping Star</a><h1 class="firstHeading">&nbsp;</h1>
      </td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">NGC 2362 Tau Canis
      Majoris Cluster</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Open cluster +
      visual double</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">4.1</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">2/14/09</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">This one
      certainly has an interesting name. It is a typical open cluster.. has
      around 60 stars and a very faint nebula surrounding it which we could not
      see.&nbsp; The brightest star, Tau Canis Majoris, is right in the center
      and shines in bright blue at magnitude 4.39. It is the brighter component
      of a spectroscopic binary. But, more interestingly, it is also part of a
      visual binary with a nearby star. We were not able to split this visual
      binary, so when looking at it, there definitely did seem to be something
      peculiar about it.. at times it appears to have an oblong shape.. due to
      the second star right nearby. This is probably why its called the &quot;Mexican
      Jumping Star&quot;.</font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mizar_(star)">Mizor and Alcor</a><h1 class="firstHeading">&nbsp;</h1>
      </td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">&quot;The Horse and
      Rider&quot;</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Visual double and
      binary</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Mizar A: .33<br>
      Mizar B:4<br>
      Alcor:3.99</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">a while ago</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Second star on
      handle of Big Dipper. This is the famous test of visual acuity. I can see
      the companion star (Alcor) under good conditions, although sometimes I
      have to tilt my glasses. In the telescope, it is easy to see that Mizor
      itself is a very close binary. </font> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_Cluster">Perseus Double
      Cluster</a><h1 class="firstHeading">&nbsp;</h1>
      </td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">NGC 884 and NGC 869</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Globular</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">4.3</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">2007</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Easy to view with 6&quot;. Only one cluster fits
      in 16&quot;, but both can be viewed easily with 3&quot; finder. </font> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NGC_457">Owl Cluster aka &quot;ET
      Cluster&quot;</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">NGC 457</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Open Cluster</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">8.4</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">11/21/08</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">This one of the
      nicest open clusters I have seen with the 16&quot;. There are several bright
      stars in an oval, and two bright stars which are the &quot;eyes&quot; of the owl or
      ET, whichever you care to imagine. There is also a rich smattering of dim
      background stars. </font> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sirius">Sirius</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43">&nbsp;</td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Multiple Star</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">-1.46</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">2/13/09</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Sirius is the
      brightest star in the night sky. It has a famous companion, &quot;the pup&quot;,
      which is a relatively dim white dwarf which is rather difficult to spot.
      The pup was predicted due to the proper motion of Sirius by the mathematician
      Bessel. We took a quick look, out of curiosity, not expecting to see it.
      Because of the glare of Sirius, the only practical way of observing the
      &quot;pup&quot; is to block Sirius just outside the edge of the eyepiece. But you
      need to know which side the pup is on. We were not able to see it, but it
      still is worth a look if you are in the neighborhood. The pup is
      currently moving away from Sirius and will be at maximum elongation in
      2025. A third component has not yet been observed visually. </font> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veil_nebula">Veil Nebula</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">NGC 6960, 6962, 6979, 6992,&nbsp; 6995</font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Nebula</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">7.0</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">8/22/08</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Large,  diffuse nebula spread through Cygnus. Observed through very nice 8 in
      telescope at ADK star party. I am not sure what part I observed, but it
      was probably the brightest loop, NGC 6960. Later tried to observe with 16&quot;
      at RPI, (9/08), the brighter half, was difficult to see anything under
      given conditions and narrow field of view, but Dave said one &quot;rope&quot; is
      usually visible passing through the brightest star. </font> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christmas_Tree_Cluster">Christmas
      Tree Cluster</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43">
    <font face="Times New Roman">
    <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christmas_Tree_Cluster">NGC 2264</a></font></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">Open Cluster and Nebula</font></td>
      <td width="6%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">2.6</font></td>
      <td width="1%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">2/13/09</font></td>
      <td width="119%" height="43"><font face="Times New Roman">The Christmas
      Tree Cluster contains the Cone Nebula, Fox Fur
      Nebula and Snowflake Cluster, however very few features are visible with
      amateur telescopes. Primarily one sees a large, sparse open cluster, which kindof sortof looks like a Christmas tree (with a bright star on top??).
      There is a one bright yellow star, which does appear to have some faint
      nebulosity around it. In actuality there are diffuse nebula filling the
      entire region. Large object, good to view in finder scope. </font> </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td width="17%" height="43">
      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacman_Nebula">PacMan Nebula</a></td>
      <td width="9%" height="43">
    NGC 281</td>
      <td width="9%" height="43">Diffuse Nebula</td>
      <td width="6%" height="43">&nbsp;</td>
      <td width="1%" height="43">&nbsp;</td>
      <td width="119%" height="43">&nbsp;</td>
    </tr>
      </table>
  </center>
</div>

    fairly small, compact object. It is supposed to be &quot;dual lobed&quot;, and while its
    too small and dim to make this out, it does appear a little unsymmetrical. </font></td>
  </tr>
</table>
</center>
